Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        The axis along which to compute the rolling median.\n        Default is -1 (the last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output shape and window alignment:\n        - 'valid': Output only where the window completely overlaps with the\n          input. Output shape will be smaller than input.\n        - 'same': Output has the same shape as the input. Windows at edges\n          are truncated.\n        - 'full': Return output for all possible window positions.\n          Output shape will be larger than input.\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians computed along the specified axis.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer, or if axis is invalid,\n        or if mode is not one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    along the array and computing the median of elements in each window.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Windows at edges\n          are truncated.\n        - 'full': Return output for all possible window positions.\n          Output shape will be larger than input.\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians computed along the specified axis.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer, or if axis is invalid,\n        or if mode is not one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    along the array and computing the median of elements in each window.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Windows at edges\n          are truncated.\n        - 'full': Return output for all possible window positions.\n          Output shape will be larger than input.\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians computed along the specified axis.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer, or if axis is invalid,\n        or if mode is not one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    along the array and computing the median of elements in each window.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Validate window_size\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)) or window_size <= 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    # Validate mode\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'\")\n\n    # Handle edge case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a\n        else:  # full\n            # Prepend and append a single element for full mode\n            return np.concatenate([a, a])\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    axis = axis % a.ndim if a.ndim > 0 else 0\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    axis_size = a.shape[axis] if a.ndim > 0 else 1\n\n    # Determine output size based on mode\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        if axis_size < window_size:\n            # Return empty array\n            output_shape = list(a.shape)\n            output_shape[axis] = 0\n            return np.empty(output_shape, dtype=a.dtype)\n        output_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        output_size = axis_size\n    else:  # full\n        output_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n\n    # Create output array\n    output_shape = list(a.shape)\n    output_shape[axis] = output_size\n    result = np.empty(output_shape, dtype=np.float64 if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    if a.ndim == 1:\n        result = _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode)\n    else:\n        # For multi-dimensional arrays, apply rolling median along the specified axis\n        # Move the target axis to the end, reshape to 2D, process, then reshape back\n        a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, -1)\n        original_moved_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n        # Reshape to 2D: (product of all dims except last, last dimension)\n        a_2d = a_moved.reshape(-1, original_moved_shape[-1])\n\n        # Process each row\n        output_rows = []\n        for row in a_2d:\n            output_rows.append(_rolling_median_1d(row, window_size, mode))\n\n        # Determine output size along the processed axis\n        if output_rows:\n            output_axis_size = len(output_rows[0])\n            # Stack the results\n            result_2d = np.vstack(output_rows)\n            # Reshape back to multi-dimensional form\n            output_moved_shape = list(original_moved_shape)\n            output_moved_shape[-1] = output_axis_size\n            result_moved = result_2d.reshape(output_moved_shape)\n            # Move axis back to original position\n            result = np.moveaxis(result_moved, -1, axis)\n        else:\n            result = np.array([])\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 1-D array.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    a : array_like\n        1-D input array\n    window_size : int\n        Size of the rolling window\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}\n        Determines output shape\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    result : ndarray\n        Rolling median values\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n    n = len(a)\n\n    result = []\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        # Standard sliding window\n        if window_size > n:\n            # Return empty array if window is larger than array\n            return np.array([], dtype=a.dtype)\n        for i in range(n - window_size + 1):\n            window = a[i:i+window_size]\n            result.append(np.median(window))\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Keep output same size as input\n        for i in range(n):\n            start = max(0, i - window_size // 2)\n            end = min(n, i + (window_size - window_size // 2))\n            window = a[start:end]\n            result.append(np.median(window))\n    else:  # full\n        # Window positions from -(window_size-1) to n-1\n        for window_start in range(-(window_size - 1), n):\n            window_end = min(n, window_start + window_size)\n            window_start_clamped = max(0, window_start)\n            window = a[window_start_clamped:window_end]\n            result.append(np.median(window))\n\n    return np.array(result, dtype=np.float64 if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":118,"oldLines":29,"newStart":118,"newLines":31,"lines":["         result = _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode)","     else:","         # {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CiCUrhU9E6MYgiduGZD1Q3","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→\"\"\"Rolling median implementation.\"\"\"\n     2→\n     3→import functools\n     4→import numpy as np\n     5→from numpy._core import overrides\n     6→\n     7→__all__ = ['rolling_median']\n     8→\n     9→array_function_dispatch = functools.partial(\n    10→    overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')\n    11→\n    12→\n    13→def _rolling_median_dispatcher(a, window_size=None, *, axis=None, mode=None):\n    14→    \"\"\"Dispatcher for rolling_median.\"\"\"\n    15→    return (a,)\n    16→\n    17→\n    18→@array_function_dispatch(_rolling_median_dispatcher)\n    19→def rolling_median(a, window_size, *, axis=-1, mode='valid'):\n    20→    \"\"\"\n    21→    Compute a rolling (sliding window) median over a 1-D array.\n    22→\n    23→    For each position in the array, computes the median of elements within\n    24→    a window centered (or aligned) at that position.\n    25→\n    26→    Parameters\n    27→    ----------\n    28→    a : array_like\n    29→        Input array or object that can be converted to an array.\n    30→    window_size : int\n    31→        The size of the rolling window. Must be a positive integer.\n    32→    axis : int, optional\n    33→        The axis along which to compute the rolling median.\n    34→        Default is -1 (the last axis).\n    35→    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n    36→        Determines the output shape and window alignment:\n    37→        - 'valid': Output only where the window completely overlaps with the\n    38→          input. Output shape will be smaller than input.\n    39→        - 'same': Output has the same shape as the input. Windows at edges\n    40→          are truncated.\n    41→        - 'full': Return output for all possible window positions.\n    42→          Output shape will be larger than input.\n    43→        Default is 'valid'.\n    44→\n    45→    Returns\n    46→    -------\n    47→    rolling_median : ndarray\n    48→        Array of rolling medians computed along the specified axis.\n    49→\n    50→    Raises\n    51→    ------\n    52→    ValueError\n    53→        If window_size is not a positive integer, or if axis is invalid,\n    54→        or if mode is not one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'.\n    55→\n    56→    Notes\n    57→    -----\n    58→    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    59→    along the array and computing the median of elements in each window.\n    60→\n    61→    Examples\n    62→    --------\n    63→    >>> import numpy as np\n    64→    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    65→    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    66→    array([2., 3., 4.])\n    67→    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    68→    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n    69→    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    70→    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    71→    \"\"\"\n    72→    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n    73→\n    74→    # Validate window_size\n    75→    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)) or window_size <= 0:\n    76→        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n    77→\n    78→    # Validate mode\n    79→    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n    80→        raise ValueError(\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full'\")\n    81→\n    82→    # Handle edge case: window_size = 1\n    83→    if window_size == 1:\n    84→        if mode == 'valid':\n    85→            return a\n    86→        elif mode == 'same':\n    87→            return a\n    88→        else:  # full\n    89→            # Prepend and append a single element for full mode\n    90→            return np.concatenate([a, a])\n    91→\n    92→    # Normalize axis\n    93→    axis = axis % a.ndim if a.ndim > 0 else 0\n    94→\n    95→    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    96→    axis_size = a.shape[axis] if a.ndim > 0 else 1\n    97→\n    98→    # Determine output size based on mode\n    99→    if mode == 'valid':\n   100→        if axis_size < window_size:\n   101→            #
